    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app',

<span id="freeTextContainer2625735157403862250">As a boy, Will Klein had a hero: his older brother, Ken. Then, on a warm suburban night in the Kleins' affluent New Jersey neighborhood, a young woman--a girl Will had once loved--was found brutally murdered in her family's basement. The prime suspect: Ken Klein. With the evidence against him overwhelming, Ken simply vanished. And when his shattered family never heard from</span>
  <span id="freeText2625735157403862250" style="display:none">As a boy, Will Klein had a hero: his older brother, Ken. Then, on a warm suburban night in the Kleins' affluent New Jersey neighborhood, a young woman--a girl Will had once loved--was found brutally murdered in her family's basement. The prime suspect: Ken Klein. With the evidence against him overwhelming, Ken simply vanished. And when his shattered family never heard from Ken again, they were sure he was gone for good. <br />Now eleven years have passed. Will has found proof that Ken is alive. And this is just the first in a series of stunning revelations as Will is forced to confront startling truths about his brother, and even himself. As a violent mystery unwinds around him, Will knows he must press his search all the way to the end. Because the most powerful surprises are yet to come.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1833037093?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Norma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Norma" href="/user/show/41400192-norma">Norma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1833037093" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6199559928994273060">GONE FOR GOOD has so many surprising twists and turns to make it another most enjoyable read by HARLAN COBEN which gets a 4.5 star rating from me!<br/><br/>I really like this authors writing style and his dialogue is terrific throughout this novel. Most of the chapters were nice and short with most having some type of revelation to keep you interested and wanting to keep turning those pages. <br/><br/>The plot was filled with lots of twists at a surprising speed that kept me totally engaged in what I was reading. I</span>
  <span id="freeText6199559928994273060" style="display:none">GONE FOR GOOD has so many surprising twists and turns to make it another most enjoyable read by HARLAN COBEN which gets a 4.5 star rating from me!<br /><br />I really like this authors writing style and his dialogue is terrific throughout this novel. Most of the chapters were nice and short with most having some type of revelation to keep you interested and wanting to keep turning those pages. <br /><br />The plot was filled with lots of twists at a surprising speed that kept me totally engaged in what I was reading. I found that it was so entertaining and fast-paced that I didn't even want to guess the outcome even though I can now see that we were given a few clues. I thought that I was given enough information on each character that it was easy to follow along with them and the storyline. <br /><br />Will Klein was my favourite character as I felt for him and was rooting for him. HARLAN COBEN actually made me feel that Will was talking directly to me, the reader!<br /><br />This book was chosen to read by me solely on who the author was. Cover, title and synopsis did not come into play on this read.<br /><br />To wrap it up it was an entertaining, enjoyable, quick and easy, fast-paced, and interesting mystery with a very satisfying ending. Would recommend!!<br /><br />Review can also be seen at Two Sisters Lost in a Coulee Reading book blog:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://twosisterslostinacoulee.com/">https://twosisterslostinacoulee.com/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6199559928994273060" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1648331808" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18231290564209558957">When I first started reading "Gone for Good" by my favourite author Harlan Coben I had to put it down as I just couldn't get into it, however having picked it up again a few days later I fully realised that it was ME and in NO WAY the book! <br/>My word! This addictive book was one helluva thriller, pace perfect it pulls you in and just doesn't let you go - I didn't want it to end and wished there had been more! There was layer upon layer of plot lines, fantastic breakneck speed twists and turns and </span>
  <span id="freeText18231290564209558957" style="display:none">When I first started reading "Gone for Good" by my favourite author Harlan Coben I had to put it down as I just couldn't get into it, however having picked it up again a few days later I fully realised that it was ME and in NO WAY the book! <br />My word! This addictive book was one helluva thriller, pace perfect it pulls you in and just doesn't let you go - I didn't want it to end and wished there had been more! There was layer upon layer of plot lines, fantastic breakneck speed twists and turns and an phenomenal ending that after having had you so tense had me emotionally wrecked! <br />I SO loved the main characters Will Klein and 'Squares' - I could see my favourite characters Win and Myron in them which made me so happy! Even a visit from Hester Crimstein - brilliant! And as for 'Ghost' - I don't think a baddie has had me so creeped out since Hannibal Lecter! <br />I wish I could give this more than 5 stars - Harlan just keeps on coming with fantastic books and plot lines - I don't know where he gets them from - but wow! this is definitely one of my favourite by Harlan (and I think I say that every time haha!). I highly recommend this book, if you've never read anything by Harlan before I urge you to start now you won't be disappointed - you'll be hooked and with so many books to read by him you'll have plenty to keep you reading! A HUGE 5 stars!!!!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="18231290564209558957" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1808756727" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1808756727" />
    <a title="P " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25327841-p"><img alt="P " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1489853536p2/25327841.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1808756727?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="P " class="user" itemprop="url" name="P " href="/user/show/25327841-p">P </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25327841-p?shelf=thriller-horror">thriller-horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1808756727" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11058569479169243636"><b>
  <blockquote>"Three days before her death, my mother told me these weren't her last words, but they were pretty close that my brother was still alive."</blockquote>
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1478939281i/21130519._SY540_.png' width='400' height='500' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Gone for Good is not so differrent from Tell No One. I was astounded how these books started off the same with the main character making an assumption that the death person is still alive. While Tell No One packs with action and gutwrenching scenes, Gone for Good is full of drama and heartbreaking stories. I enjoyed Gone for Good since the first few chapte</span>
  <span id="freeText11058569479169243636" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote>"Three days before her death, my mother told me these weren't her last words, but they were pretty close that my brother was still alive."</blockquote>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1478939281i/21130519._SY540_.png" width="400" height="500" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Gone for Good is not so differrent from Tell No One. I was astounded how these books started off the same with the main character making an assumption that the death person is still alive. While Tell No One packs with action and gutwrenching scenes, Gone for Good is full of drama and heartbreaking stories. I enjoyed Gone for Good since the first few chapters, but after various characters come out of nowhere, I got the feeling that this book was hard to concentrate about who each one is or who takes a part in the crime. Can't deny that Coben is a smart writer, he hid the evidences in the evidences, and the twists were likewise profound and cruel that made me frown so many times.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1478939398i/21130533.jpg" width="400" height="250" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>The Ghost stood. "I didn't come back for revenge or even justice,"</blockquote>
</b><br><br>Will Klein is my favorite character, it was fun to hear what he knows. His thought is not messy, and his sympathy for other people gives this book a family vibe at the same time. Ken Klein is also an interesting one, even he doesn't take many parts in this book, it still intrigued me when Will thinks of his brother and wholeheartedly hope that he's still alive.<br><br><b>
  <u>But why 3 stars ?</u>
</b><br><br>As I said, this book is very much alike Tell No One but lacks of action scenes. Although that's not the problem for me, the problem is the characters are too much and they made me confused. Some characters just pop up and disappear, I am so curious that it would be better if Coben limited his characters as few as possible. And the ending was just so-so, not mind-blowing like Tell No One.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431215580ra/14806455.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>By the way, it's a great read for me. I have many of his books on my shelves right now.<br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://goo.gl/XyvWNf">https://goo.gl/XyvWNf</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11058569479169243636" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1946138979" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1946138979" />
    <a title="Margitte" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7481492-margitte"><img alt="Margitte" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1361772481p2/7481492.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1946138979?book_show_action=true">Mar 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Margitte" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Margitte" href="/user/show/7481492-margitte">Margitte</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780307422989" href="/book/show/7136564-gone-for-good">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=family-sagas">family-sagas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=crime-novel">crime-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=american-author">american-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=2017-read">2017-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=american-novel">american-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=drama">drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1946138979" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14622349281861230094">FROM THE BLURB<br/><i>As a boy, Will Klein had a hero: his older brother, Ken. Then, on a warm suburban night in the Kleins’ affluent New Jersey neighborhood, a young woman—a girl Will had once loved—was found brutally murdered in her family’s basement. The prime suspect: Ken Klein. With the evidence against him overwhelming, Ken simply vanished. And when his shattered family never heard from Ken again, they were sure he was gone for good.<br/><br/>Now eleven years have passed. Will has found proof that Ken is al</i></span>
  <span id="freeText14622349281861230094" style="display:none">FROM THE BLURB<br /><i>As a boy, Will Klein had a hero: his older brother, Ken. Then, on a warm suburban night in the Kleins’ affluent New Jersey neighborhood, a young woman—a girl Will had once loved—was found brutally murdered in her family’s basement. The prime suspect: Ken Klein. With the evidence against him overwhelming, Ken simply vanished. And when his shattered family never heard from Ken again, they were sure he was gone for good.<br /><br />Now eleven years have passed. Will has found proof that Ken is alive. And this is just the first in a series of stunning revelations as Will is forced to confront startling truths about his brother—and himself. As a violent mystery unwinds around him, Will knows that he must press his search all the way to the end. Because the most powerful surprises are yet to come.</i><br /><br />As the author says, <i> ...the thing about clichés is that they're dead on.</i> I can so live with that. Some of them made good sense in this book.<br /><br />I loveeeeeeed this murder mystery, suspense thriller. Messing around with the sleuthing readers, the author knew where to pull the punches to get us disorientated and lost on the wrong tracks of facts. Surprise after surprise! Oh myyyyyy, it was brilliant.<br /><br />Trivial things delighted me, such as the normalcy of their lives. They engaged in ordinary things, eating salads, cheese omelettes, home or french fries, and enjoy venti iced lattés or frappuccinos. It was necessary to escape the stark reality of murder, betrayal, revenge and destroyed lives. <br /><br />Ken Klein had been the fiery tennis player, John Asselta the psycho wrestler, McGuane the wow-'em charmer and student council president. Three friends, natives and products from the Livingston suburb, New Jersey. Popular, intelligent, ambitious. <br /><br />Whatever could go wrong in these three friends' lives, when the well-watered lawns, split-level constructed homes, Little Leagues, soccer moms, piano lessons, Four Squares courts, and parent-teacher conferences, acted as some sort of wolfsbane to supposedly ward of evil?<br /><br />Evil was suppose to manifest in jails, where a melting pot of people were captured: a potpourri of inhumanity that inhabits this mini-United Nations. Ten different languages could be heard at the same time. There were shades of skin color that could inspire the people at Crayola. There were baseball caps and turbans and toupees and even a fez. <br /><br />Into this Crayola of colorful cultures, characters such as Yogi Squares the Yoga guru could be found. And Sheila, Nora, Katy, Wanda, Agents Fisher and Joey Pistillo. A place like Covenant house could exist where young teenagers were safely rescued from the streets.<br /><br />All of them had their stories to tell. A twist of fate brought them all together in the hunt for truth and reconciliation. Some lost. Some won. Nobody walked away unscathed. <blockquote>
  <b>"The ugliest of truths, in the end, was still better than the prettiest of lies."</b>
</blockquote>A fantastic read! It was as much an emotional fairground parade as it was a Bruce Springsteen concert of mayhem and revolt. Even the reader got caught up in the fast moving rhythms of a mesmerized trance. The suspense was <i>that</i> good. The ending amazing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14622349281861230094" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6877183570614361462">Will Klein's character is marvelous. This story had more twists and turns than words can convey, maybe a few too many, which is why I'm giving it four stars rather than five. To write a synopsis of this book would be damned near impossible because of allllllllllll that's going on.<br/><br/>The basic premise is that as a young man, Will is close to his girlfriend and his older brother, up until the point where his girlfriend breaks up with him. A year later, she is found strangled to death, and his older b</span>
  <span id="freeText6877183570614361462" style="display:none">Will Klein's character is marvelous. This story had more twists and turns than words can convey, maybe a few too many, which is why I'm giving it four stars rather than five. To write a synopsis of this book would be damned near impossible because of allllllllllll that's going on.<br /><br />The basic premise is that as a young man, Will is close to his girlfriend and his older brother, up until the point where his girlfriend breaks up with him. A year later, she is found strangled to death, and his older brother named as the murderer. His older brother, Ken, flees, and is thought to be dead, until one day a mysterious picture is discovered amongst his mother's things shortly after her death. The picture is of Ken! <br /><br />We follow Will through the dangerous underworld of New York City, searching for answers. Did his brother die? Did he murder his ex-girlfriend, Julie? All this and more slowly unravels. <br /><br />I had never read Harlan Coben before this book, but I'll be sure to go back and find a few of his other gems to read. I was impressed.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/194261927" />
    <a title="Vivian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3947172-vivian"><img alt="Vivian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1458107851p2/3947172.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/194261927?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vivian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vivian" href="/user/show/3947172-vivian">Vivian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947172-vivian?shelf=2018-odyssey">2018-odyssey</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947172-vivian?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947172-vivian?shelf=library">library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer194261927" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11855008198380896694">Salacious suspense. This reads like a tawdry daytime soap opera, but with a higher body count.<br/><br/>So, this happened. It wasn't bad, but the new character every chapter and ever-increasing slide into moral turpitude in this Disturbia Hell came across heavy-handed and spectacle driven. There was a decoupage mentality to the reveal of the storyline by pasting on a new "shocking" aka wildly stereotypical development. <br/><br/>Subtle it is not. <br/><br/>There were some great underlying themes like face value, redemption, </span>
  <span id="freeText11855008198380896694" style="display:none">Salacious suspense. This reads like a tawdry daytime soap opera, but with a higher body count.<br /><br />So, this happened. It wasn't bad, but the new character every chapter and ever-increasing slide into moral turpitude in this Disturbia Hell came across heavy-handed and spectacle driven. There was a decoupage mentality to the reveal of the storyline by pasting on a new "shocking" aka wildly stereotypical development. <br /><br />Subtle it is not. <br /><br />There were some great underlying themes like face value, redemption, and sacrifice, but they got lost under the excess of plot and characters. The only thing which sat there sedately was the setting which is only funny because I have family and friends scattered all over New Jersey so Fair Lawn--yep, Livingston-yep. Where's Livingston? Near Nutley. Where's Nutley? Near Livingston. And that everyone's inside everyone else's back pocket is an excellent reason why I would rather rip out toenails than move back East, again.<br /><br />If you're looking for a popcorn thriller suspense, then you could do far worse than this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11855008198380896694" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_14548944" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/14548944" />
    <a title="Sam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/626425-sam"><img alt="Sam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1203825409p2/626425.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

<span id="freeTextContainer406493599089837328">Coben is the King of the Plot Twist. Gone for Good is first of Harlan Coben's many novels that I have read and this one drew me is so much that I read it all in one day. Each chapter ends with a cliff hanger and that makes you want to keep reading. He also does a fantastic job of character development. If you enjoy a good mystery that will keep up on the edge and always guessing...I suggest Gone For Good. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4008202182921059236">There is no getting away from it Harlan Coben knows how to enthral his readers.<br/>This was heading for a 5/5 star review until, that is, I got to the end. The end was a real let down and for that reason it got 4/5 stars. But the other 90% was a nail bitter.<br/><br/>Will Klein is a quiet, unassuming young man but a young man who has seen more than his fair share of trouble. People that are special to him keep dying.   <span id="freeText4008202182921059236" style="display:none">There is no getting away from it Harlan Coben knows how to enthral his readers.<br />This was heading for a 5/5 star review until, that is, I got to the end. The end was a real let down and for that reason it got 4/5 stars. But the other 90% was a nail bitter.<br /><br />Will Klein is a quiet, unassuming young man but a young man who has seen more than his fair share of trouble. People that are special to him keep dying. His first true love in murdered and the bother he idolises is accused for her death. The brother disappears before the police can arrest him and a dark cloud descends over the family, now known as the family of a murderer. The family cling to the belief that the brother was set up.<br /><br />Eleven years on and Will’s second love has just walked out on him. It’s not long before Will gets news that his now girlfriend is also dead. This is just too much to be a coincidence.<br /><br />Will decides that if he is to discover what is going on he will have to go back eleven years to get the answers he needs. The brother he so idolised turns out not to be the brother Will thought he was.<br /><br />Harlan Coben is the master of the dead end sub plots. Nobody is who you think they are. The pace is full on and there are enough vile characters to make you want vengeance most foul. <br /><br />That said the end is a let down.<br /><br />Recommended for adrenaline junkies.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15967353980802357598">This was my first experience with Harlan Coben and I don't think I'm clamoring to read another. I didn't hate this. It was good enough entertainment for a couple of days. But I can't recommend it.<br/><br/>Characters are one-dimensional. But they almost have to be. Revealing too much of each character wouldn't allow Harlan Coben to change what all the characters are and what they stand for and what they'r emotivated by in the last twenty pages.   <span id="freeText15967353980802357598" style="display:none">This was my first experience with Harlan Coben and I don't think I'm clamoring to read another. I didn't hate this. It was good enough entertainment for a couple of days. But I can't recommend it.<br /><br />Characters are one-dimensional. But they almost have to be. Revealing too much of each character wouldn't allow Harlan Coben to change what all the characters are and what they stand for and what they'r emotivated by in the last twenty pages. Seriously, this was one of those novels where a new revelation happens every two pages for the entire span of the last forty pages. No, I'm not a good guy. I'm the bad guy! So am I! So is she! I was just joshing. I'm a good guy! I've been hiding my motivation all along so that I can pull this gun out and shoot the real bad guy! <br /><br />With that said, Coben's plot has a break-neck pace. I appreciated that. It made the whole affair finish up that much faster. </span>

<div id="review_332746897" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/332746897" />
    <a title="Greg Bascom" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9612959-greg-bascom"><img alt="Greg Bascom" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1337357693p2/9612959.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/332746897?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Greg Bascom" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Greg Bascom" href="/user/show/9612959-greg-bascom">Greg Bascom</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer332746897" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14862352974948759608">GONE FOR GOOD is a fast paced thriller with at least 60 plot twists, turns or startling revelations (I catalogued them.) Typical of the genre, it is plot rather than character driven. Even the best characters are a bit shallow, and you will have to accept some improbable ones. Dialogue is written well. Otherwise, the writing is simple - if you got through third grade you won't need a dictionary - although after some stretches of short choppy sentences and dangling phrases you might wish for some</span>
  <span id="freeText14862352974948759608" style="display:none">GONE FOR GOOD is a fast paced thriller with at least 60 plot twists, turns or startling revelations (I catalogued them.) Typical of the genre, it is plot rather than character driven. Even the best characters are a bit shallow, and you will have to accept some improbable ones. Dialogue is written well. Otherwise, the writing is simple - if you got through third grade you won't need a dictionary - although after some stretches of short choppy sentences and dangling phrases you might wish for something more mature. There is unnecessary violence and implausibility both of character and event. Again, that seems typical of the genre.<br /><br />The story is fast paced not just because the author uses cliff hanging chapter endings and plot twists. He dribbles out information. First there is a limousine, then a man in the back seat, then a man sitting next to him, then a driver, then the relationship suggesting they are hoods, and then finally they are. You have to turn pages to get this. Another technique is to insert a short chapter of a seemingly unrelated event, an incomplete scene, and leave it to be developed later, maybe much later. Also, Coben will interleave chapters with two or more related plot elements as he develops the story.<br /><br />This is a four star read in the thriller genre - put "thriller genre" in bold italics and underline it. The reviewers who did not like this novel, in general, dislike violent thrillers without well developed characters. A few who do read thrillers found the plot too much like Coben's first thriller, TELL NO ONE. I agree with that.<br /><br />TELL NO ONE opened with a juxtaposition of love and tragedy that was well done and grabbed me in the gut, as it did many other reviewers. As I read GONE FOR GOOD, I wanted to feel the relationship between Will and Sheila, but it wasn't there. That disappointed. For me, the ending in TELL NO ONE was, to be diplomatic, moronic. As I read the startling ending of GONE FOR GOOD, it seemed too far over the top, but when I got to the one page epilogue, my stomach settled and I smiled</span>
  <a data-text-id="14862352974948759608" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2895663477?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marty Fried" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marty Fried" href="/user/show/8530205-marty-fried">Marty Fried</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9780736686945" href="/book/show/469619.Gone_for_Good">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8530205-marty-fried?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8530205-marty-fried?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8530205-marty-fried?shelf=brutal">brutal</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2895663477" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14353446902116822372">What a roller-coaster! Or maybe I should compare it to an etch-a-sketch (if anyone remembers these) where you often need to shake it up and start over. Every time you think you know what happened, the world tilts, and it's all wrong - all the way to the very end. Bad guys become good guys, good guys become bad guys, minor characters become important, etc. The worst bad guy started out as a promising young good guy, and gradually became very sadistic, although mainly to lawyers, so perhaps he tho</span>
  <span id="freeText14353446902116822372" style="display:none">What a roller-coaster! Or maybe I should compare it to an etch-a-sketch (if anyone remembers these) where you often need to shake it up and start over. Every time you think you know what happened, the world tilts, and it's all wrong - all the way to the very end. Bad guys become good guys, good guys become bad guys, minor characters become important, etc. The worst bad guy started out as a promising young good guy, and gradually became very sadistic, although mainly to lawyers, so perhaps he thought he was being a good guy.<br /><br />There were a lot of very interesting characters in the book, if you can keep up with who's who. All in all, this book made me remember how much I like Coben's books. I'm glad there are a lot more to read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14353446902116822372" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1150931463" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1150931463" />
    <a title="David" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18614687-david"><img alt="David" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442655902p2/18614687.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1150931463?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David" href="/user/show/18614687-david">David</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1150931463" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15495906248767725942">My first Harlan Coben book and will definitely not be my last.<br/><br/>I just love the way Harlan Coben writes. I think most authors struggle to pull of writing in the second person but you feel like Harlan's having a conversation with you - the Reader - as you read this book.<br/><br/>It's a story with many twists and turns and jut remember that nothing is ever as it seems.<br/><br/>Our protagonist has struggled to clear his brother's name for most of his life. His brother has been framed as the killer of a girl he used to</span>
  <span id="freeText15495906248767725942" style="display:none">My first Harlan Coben book and will definitely not be my last.<br /><br />I just love the way Harlan Coben writes. I think most authors struggle to pull of writing in the second person but you feel like Harlan's having a conversation with you - the Reader - as you read this book.<br /><br />It's a story with many twists and turns and jut remember that nothing is ever as it seems.<br /><br />Our protagonist has struggled to clear his brother's name for most of his life. His brother has been framed as the killer of a girl he used to love. The police force think his brother's guilty. The local community thinks his brother is guilty. The deceased's family think his brother is guilty. Even his parents harbour doubts about his brother's innocence. Still, Will believes his brother - Kevin Klein - is innocent. His brother goes on the run and for many years, it'd appear his gone for good and never to come back.<br /><br />Will's mother whispers something on her deathbed that sets his world upside down and opens a can of worms.<br /><br />I liked how Harlan made Will Klein so vulnerable. You feel for him and wish him all the best. You wish him well but it seems his best intentions only hurt those around him and lead him to dead ends. Will discovers himself in the end and the truth sets him free.<br /><br />A worthy addition to your library.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15495906248767725942" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11250037482800977172">Yet another loved-one-presumed-dead-but-look-may-still-be-alive-and-in-hiding story from Harlan Coben. I'm about 25% through, and may ditch it. Same story, different book.<br/><br/>UPDATE: I'm out. Made it halfway through, but it just wasn't worth reading any further.</span>

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1414967071" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2115747540975691467"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43933.Tell_No_One' title='Tell No One by Harlan Coben' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tell No One</a> was my first Harlan Coben novel and IMHO it was an amazing tale. Coben is clearly a gifted writer, with a good sense of what it takes to grab your interest and hook you, and then keep you going until the last page .... and then some. <br/><br/>However, having started with Tell No One, Gone for Good seemed like a reformulation. Hero is a grieving man whose beloved family member is dead ..... or are they? Check. Psychotic killer using grossly innovative ways to kill? Check. Gung-ho law enforceme</span>
  <span id="freeText2115747540975691467" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43933.Tell_No_One" title="Tell No One by Harlan Coben" rel="nofollow noopener">Tell No One</a> was my first Harlan Coben novel and IMHO it was an amazing tale. Coben is clearly a gifted writer, with a good sense of what it takes to grab your interest and hook you, and then keep you going until the last page .... and then some. <br /><br />However, having started with Tell No One, Gone for Good seemed like a reformulation. Hero is a grieving man whose beloved family member is dead ..... or are they? Check. Psychotic killer using grossly innovative ways to kill? Check. Gung-ho law enforcement types convinced the hero knows more? Check. Fascinating no nonsense side-kick? Check. Toss in a few improbable coincidences and there you go. <br /><br />I would give "Gone for Good" three-and-a-half stars because it WAS a really good read, but the plot seemed a bit too similar, and I wish the main characters (in each book) had been a bit-more fleshed out and developed. Of course, your results may vary .......</span>
  <a data-text-id="2115747540975691467" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1961240553259722165">I just finished this book and I feel like I've gone on a hell of a roller coaster ride without even leaving home. WOW! This book was absolutely incredible! Every time I thought I had it figured out, Coben came up with another twist to make me question my theories or spin them into nothing but complete chaos.   <span id="freeText1961240553259722165" style="display:none">I just finished this book and I feel like I've gone on a hell of a roller coaster ride without even leaving home. WOW! This book was absolutely incredible! Every time I thought I had it figured out, Coben came up with another twist to make me question my theories or spin them into nothing but complete chaos. The man is absolutely genius when it comes to thinking up plot twists and turns to keeping the reader second-guessing. <br /><br />If you like a book that will keep you guessing all the way to the very last page, then run - don't walk - to your nearest library or book store and get your hands on this book! If you want something a little more sedate and bland, then you may wish to just leave this book alone because once you start reading, you won't be able to stop -- just like when you strap in to a real roller coaster ride.</span>

  <span id="freeText12967941055193032554" style="display:none">The absolute best H.C. novel to date and that's saying something. The plots, subplots, sub-sub plots are endless and will probably keep you guessing. However, I did figure this one out early on haha, then changed my mind a bit later, and then after a while decided on a different direction, and finally found myself out in left-field out of smokes with an empty beer can. <br />What can I say? A very clever story with so many subtle twists and turns, gut wrenching and spine tingling one moment and somber and heartfelt the next. I kinda felt sorry for our protagonist Will (by the way, why are the good guys always named Will?), but he showed he had the testicular fortitude to challenge the evil powers that be which at the time seemed virtually impossible. <br />Moving on back to another protagonist and good guy named Will, this time Will Trent #1 'Triptych' for a second time.</span>

<div id="review_3488330217" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3488330217" />
    <a title="Soham Ghosh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/89399061-soham-ghosh"><img alt="Soham Ghosh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583923430p2/89399061.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3488330217?book_show_action=true">Aug 10, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Soham Ghosh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Soham Ghosh" href="/user/show/89399061-soham-ghosh">Soham Ghosh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/89399061-soham-ghosh?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/89399061-soham-ghosh?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3488330217" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11832791378431890619">From the mind that gave us <i>Tell No One</i>, comes <i>Trust No One</i>...oops, sorry...<i>Gone For Good</i>. I really wanted to be blown away by this, but for some reason, my feet failed to leave the ground.<br/><br/>Don't get me wrong, it's a brilliantly-crafted mystery, with more twists than you can ever be prepared for, despite being warned beforehand by the review that (accurately) claims that it has "more twists and turns than an amusement park ride". Yet, there is something lacking here that that I cannot exactly put </span>
  <span id="freeText11832791378431890619" style="display:none">From the mind that gave us <i>Tell No One</i>, comes <i>Trust No One</i>...oops, sorry...<i>Gone For Good</i>. I really wanted to be blown away by this, but for some reason, my feet failed to leave the ground.<br /><br />Don't get me wrong, it's a brilliantly-crafted mystery, with more twists than you can ever be prepared for, despite being warned beforehand by the review that (accurately) claims that it has "more twists and turns than an amusement park ride". Yet, there is something lacking here that that I cannot exactly put my finger on. I figured that the best way I can try to approach what I feel about this book, is by comparing it to <i>Tell No One</i>. I have rated both 4 stars, but for entirely different reasons. I had thoroughly enjoyed every bit of <i>Tell No One</i> and I had so badly wanted to give it a 5-star rating, but it wasn't worthy of that, because the unnecessary twist on the final page had practically ruined an otherwise masterfully-woven mystery, opening up a Pandora's Box of plot-holes and inconsistencies. On the other hand, <i>Gone For Good</i>'s final twist (which, again, comes on the very last page), or any of the countless twists, for that matter, does not derail the plot one bit, and the story wraps up perfectly, leaving no loose ends. This one deserves a 5-star rating, but I couldn't bring myself to enjoy it enough to give it one. <br /><br />The principal narrator is Will Klein, whose elder brother Ken is an international fugitive who has been on the run from the law after being charged with the murder of Julie Miller eleven years ago. After all these years of presuming Ken to be dead, Will learns that Ken might be alive after all. When Will's girlfriend Sheila disappears and her fingerprints turn up at a murder scene, all hell breaks loose, and Will learns one shocking secret after another about the people in his life, which makes me suspect that Harlan Coben has major trust issues. So yeah, "Trust No One", Willie boy. <br /><br />Now, unlike <i>Tell No One</i>, the plotting is practically flawless this time, with no narrative inconsistencies whatsoever, except for the slight suspension of disbelief that a Harlan Coben story usually requires. However, for some reason which I cannot articulate properly, I failed to feel the tension in the story. I also couldn't bring myself to care much about the protagonist, Will, who is largely a passive character here, who does little more than serve as our eyes. Maybe these problems could have been avoided, had the writing been better, like in the beautifully-written <i>Tell No One</i>, which, alas, had plotting-problems. Or, perhaps, the only reason behind my slight disappointment with <i>Gone For Good</i> was the constant subconscious comparison with <i>Tell No One</i>. Nevertheless, <i>Gone For Good</i> is a great and thoroughly unpredictable mystery with too many WTF twists to count. No matter how much experience you've had with mysteries or thrillers, you simply cannot guess where a Harlan Coben story is going next, until Coben takes you there himself.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11832791378431890619" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_351307093" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/351307093" />
    <a title="Best Crime Books &amp; More" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10323950-best-crime-books-more"><img alt="Best Crime Books &amp; More" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1433946891p2/10323950.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/351307093?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Best Crime Books &amp; More" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Best Crime Books &amp; More" href="/user/show/10323950-best-crime-books-more">Best Crime Books &amp; More</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer351307093" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16205551985329647167">I have read one of Harlan Coben's stand alone novels, albeit some time ago, and am slowly working my way through his back catalogue. In this book we meet Will Klein and I found that it didn't take long for me to like him. What also became apparent pretty quickly was that Will Klein is an ordinary bloke. He isn't somebody who can ruthlessly take down bad guys and he isn't a brooding lead character that has an issue with authority. In other words, a welcome change from the ordinary leading male co</span>
  <span id="freeText16205551985329647167" style="display:none">I have read one of Harlan Coben's stand alone novels, albeit some time ago, and am slowly working my way through his back catalogue. In this book we meet Will Klein and I found that it didn't take long for me to like him. What also became apparent pretty quickly was that Will Klein is an ordinary bloke. He isn't somebody who can ruthlessly take down bad guys and he isn't a brooding lead character that has an issue with authority. In other words, a welcome change from the ordinary leading male cop type character!<br /><br />The story itself is quite interesting and before long you realise that the disappearance of Will's girlfriend is far from ordinary. There is also the added plot thread that includes the disappearance of Wills brother who is trhe main suspect in the murder of Julie Miller 11 years prior.<br /><br />One of the things that really struck me with the Myron Bolitar series of books was the great characters, this book was no different. Will Klein's friend Squares is a brilliant added character and I found that I would have like to have actually seen more of him in the book. Even with that as a negative this book was still an absolutely brilliant read.<br /><br />Towards the end I found myself reading even quicker and I must say that the last few chapters had many twists and surprises in store which I absolutely loved. All in all it was another winner from Harlan Coben. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16205551985329647167" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="David" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5547564-david"><img alt="David" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514512968p2/5547564.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/187628209?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David" href="/user/show/5547564-david">David</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5547564-david?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5547564-david?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer187628209" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7093241098291997675">Coben takes a good plot and suspense, but taints it with cardboard characters and too much suspension of belief. The humorous first person which I normally love seems to only work part of the time. Will, the protagonist seems to have only two traits: irrationally angry and hopelessly naive (you know, when another character is trying to explain a formulaic plot twist that you as the reader saw through five minutes earlier, but he just can't wrap his head around it.) The only interesting character</span>
  <span id="freeText7093241098291997675" style="display:none">Coben takes a good plot and suspense, but taints it with cardboard characters and too much suspension of belief. The humorous first person which I normally love seems to only work part of the time. Will, the protagonist seems to have only two traits: irrationally angry and hopelessly naive (you know, when another character is trying to explain a formulaic plot twist that you as the reader saw through five minutes earlier, but he just can't wrap his head around it.) The only interesting character is one of the antagonists, the Ghost, and even he is dulled down by the end. With the plot and pacing, I might have rated this one higher if I hadn't recently read so many superior books lately, including thrillers. This is your literary equivalent of a Lifetime Movie Network original.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7093241098291997675" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_15335946" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/15335946" />
    <a title="Jeanette (Again)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/796425-jeanette-again"><img alt="Jeanette (Again)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1304653755p2/796425.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/15335946?book_show_action=true">Feb 13, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeanette (Again)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeanette (Again)" href="/user/show/796425-jeanette-again">Jeanette (Again)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/796425-jeanette-again?shelf=four-star-fiction">four-star-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/796425-jeanette-again?shelf=suspense-thriller">suspense-thriller</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer15335946" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11312359758466381671">"The truth is, we are mere animals, organisms, even, slightly more complex than your basic paramecium. You die, you're gone. It was pure megalomania to think we humans are somehow above death, that we, unlike any other creature, have the ability to transcend it. In life, sure, we are special, dominant, because we are the strongest and most ruthless. We rule. But in death, to believe that we are somehow special in God's eyes, that we can worm our way into his good graces by kissing his ass, well,</span>
  <span id="freeText11312359758466381671" style="display:none">"The truth is, we are mere animals, organisms, even, slightly more complex than your basic paramecium. You die, you're gone. It was pure megalomania to think we humans are somehow above death, that we, unlike any other creature, have the ability to transcend it. In life, sure, we are special, dominant, because we are the strongest and most ruthless. We rule. But in death, to believe that we are somehow special in God's eyes, that we can worm our way into his good graces by kissing his ass, well, that's the sort of thinking that the rich have used to keep the poor in place since the beginning of man's rule." </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer746542622" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1583053921473186974">I love this author. I've read many a book by him. This is a crime/mystery book and I liked this one. I loved all the twists, especially the unexpected ones at the end. It was well done. Harlan also does a great job with his characters....and most of them are incredibly likable. I like when I care about them, especially Will. So 4 stars.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2805987291?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin (from Long Island, NY)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin (from Long Island, NY)" href="/user/show/58787538-erin-from-long-island-ny">Erin (from Long Island, NY)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2805987291" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer295157084541268730">Wow! So this was my first by Harlan Coben & i don't know how I've missed him all these years! Let me start by saying that i do love current storylines.. I love when books have aspects of say social media & cell phones, even current social issues. So sometimes i hesitate when a book is older.. That needn't have worried me with this 1! Over 15 years old & it didn't feel dated at all, i really enjoyed it. I loved the main character Will.. & his best friend "Squares" so much- i seriously wish there </span>
  <span id="freeText295157084541268730" style="display:none">Wow! So this was my first by Harlan Coben &amp; i don't know how I've missed him all these years! Let me start by saying that i do love current storylines.. I love when books have aspects of say social media &amp; cell phones, even current social issues. So sometimes i hesitate when a book is older.. That needn't have worried me with this 1! Over 15 years old &amp; it didn't feel dated at all, i really enjoyed it. I loved the main character Will.. &amp; his best friend "Squares" so much- i seriously wish there more books with these 2! Actually the "bad" guys were pretty intense too. I won't soon forget "the ghost!" The atmosphere was great. I really appreciated the way the author described and empathized with the runaways and just the whole street life, it added so much. Really, really good story.. Lots of twists. I suppose some suspension of belief may be needed, but the storytelling is so good it didn't even occur to me at the time! I'd still recommend this book today &amp; knowing i have so many more from this author is such a treat! </span>
  <a data-text-id="295157084541268730" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('pSTXAtMMclyjARIrB7glawDtlx1DmKjyb+REHhZm3YpLrrkNacFDNohAbOe6c/eNrMkvJrC5p1JP+60qJ7zzuQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0L4OE6ex8qXEwFLJ8OvoaXGpTJh7IDGoM0UobMXVLKw+NGAcHXzDz++BLAVNIDqP3Y30o4gBPggTWsFY9A8Cnw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

কাপুতে নাকি একসময় নরবলী হতো। নদীর তলদেশে এখনো কঙ্কাল, মানুষের মাথার খুলি মিলে। মিলে জং ধরা গিলোটিন। কাপুত নদীর ওপর সেতু বানানো হচ্ছে। এই ডামাডোলের মাঝে পরপর ছয়জন বাচ্চার খণ্ডিত মৃতদেহ উদ্ধার করা হয়। লাশগুলোর কপালের ঠিক নিচে, দুই চোখ যেখানে ছিল সেখানে দুইটা গোল চাকতির মতো গর্ত। ছয়টা লাশেরই পাঁজর ভাঙ্গা, হৃৎপিন্ড উপড়ানো!\n\n\n  চোখের বদলে নিকষ কালো আঁধার ফ্যালফ্যাল করে তাকিয়ে সেঁটে দিয়েছে। কিন্তু সে তো বহুদিন ধরেই নিশ্চুপ। তবে কী বেশ পাল্টে পুনরায় ফিরে এসেছে খুনী? আবারো কী ভয়ংকর নৃশংসতায় মাতবে বিশ্বচরাচর?\n\nনাম তার বিঘতখানেক লম্বা। সৈয়দ শাহ ফতেহ গিল। দাদা আদর করে When Amos Decker and his FBI colleague Alex Jamison are called to London, North Dakota, they instantly sense that the thriving fracking town is ripe for trouble. The promise of a second gold rush has attracted an onslaught of newcomers all hoping for a windfall, and the community is growing faster than houses can be built. The sudden boom has also brought a slew of problems with it, including drugs, property crimes, prostitution -- and now murder.Decker and Jamison are ordered to investigate the death of a young woman named Irene Cramer, whose body was expertly autopsied and then dumped in the open -- which is only the beginning of the oddities surrounding the case. As Decker and Jamison dig into Irene\'s life, they are shocked to discover that the woman who walked the streets by night as a prostitute was a teacher for a local religious sect by day -- a sect operating on land once owned by a mysterious government facility that looms over the entire community.London is a town replete with ruthless business owners, shady government officials, and religious outsiders, all determined to keep their secrets from coming out. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8264981930294974043">With over 60 million books in print worldwide, Harlan Coben’s last seven consecutive novels, MISSING YOU, SIX YEARS, STAY CLOSE, LIVE WIRE, CAUGHT, LONG LOST and HOLD TIGHT all debuted at #1 on the <i>New York Times</i> bestseller list and lists around the world. His books are published in 43 languages around the globe.<br/><br/>Coben is the winner of the Edgar Award, Shamus Award and Anthony Award – the first aut</span>
  <span id="freeText8264981930294974043" style="display:none">With over 60 million books in print worldwide, Harlan Coben’s last seven consecutive novels, MISSING YOU, SIX YEARS, STAY CLOSE, LIVE WIRE, CAUGHT, LONG LOST and HOLD TIGHT all debuted at #1 on the <i>New York Times</i> bestseller list and lists around the world. His books are published in 43 languages around the globe.<br /><br />Coben is the winner of the Edgar Award, Shamus Award and Anthony Award – the first author to win all three – and he has received an eclectic variety of honors from all over the world. His novel TELL NO ONE has been turned into a hit French film of the same name. His essays and columns have appeared in many top publications. <br /><br />Harlan was born in Newark, New Jersey. He still lives in New Jersey with his wife, Anne Armstrong-Coben MD, a pediatrician, and their four children.<br /></span>
